## 🎓 TEACHING RULES — HOW TO EXPLAIN THINGS

These rules are **non-negotiable**. Every code response MUST follow them.

### Rule T1 — Explain Before Code
Before showing ANY new Kotlin/Python/Bash code that uses a concept the developer hasn't seen before:
- Write a plain-English explanation (2-4 sentences) of WHAT the concept is
- Write a simple real-life analogy (e.g., "Hilt is like a restaurant kitchen that prepares ingredients before a chef needs them — so the chef (ViewModel) doesn't have to go shopping himself")
- THEN show the code

### Rule T2 — Line-by-Line Comments (MANDATORY)
**Every single line of code you write MUST have a comment explaining what it does.**
This rule applies to:
- Kotlin Android code
- Python server/scraping code
- Bash/shell scripts
- Docker Compose YAML
- Gradle build files
- XML files (if any)
- JSON config files

**Comment style:**
```kotlin
// ✅ CORRECT — beginner-friendly comment style
val micButton = remember { mutableStateOf(false) }
// ^ 'remember' keeps this value alive across Compose redraws (like a sticky note on the screen)
// ^ 'mutableStateOf(false)' creates a true/false value that starts as 'false' (mic is OFF)
// ^ When this value changes, Jetpack Compose automatically redraws the mic button
```

```python
# ✅ CORRECT — Python comment style
qdrant_client = QdrantClient(host="localhost", port=6333)
# ^ QdrantClient is the Python library that lets us talk to the Qdrant vector database
# ^ host="localhost" means Qdrant is running on the same machine as this Python script
# ^ port=6333 is the door number (port) that Qdrant listens on — like a phone extension
```

```yaml
# ✅ CORRECT — Docker Compose comment style
services:          # 'services' lists all the programs (containers) we want to run
  fastapi:         # This is our main Python web server — handles all Android app requests
    image: python:3.11-slim   # Use Python 3.11 slim (small) Docker image as the base
    ports:
      - "8000:8000"  # Map port 8000 on Ubuntu to port 8000 inside the container
                     # Format: "HOST_PORT:CONTAINER_PORT"
                     # Android app sends requests to Ubuntu:8000 → reaches FastAPI inside Docker
```

### Rule T3 — Teach File Placement
Whenever you create a new file, always state:
- What folder it goes in
- Why it goes there
- How it relates to other files already created

Example:
```
📁 File: app/src/main/java/com/rushdululilm/app/ui/screens/HomeScreen.kt
   Why here: Android Studio looks for UI screens in the 'ui/screens/' folder by convention.
             'com.rushdululilm.app' matches the package name we set in build.gradle.
   Relates to: MainActivity.kt (which calls this screen), NavGraph.kt (which routes to it)
```

### Rule T4 — Show the Full Picture First
Before writing code for any new feature:
1. Show a simple diagram (ASCII or text) of how the feature connects to other parts
2. List ALL files that will be created or modified
3. Estimate how long it will take to understand and implement
4. Then write the code file by file, top to bottom

---

## 🚫 ANTI-HALLUCINATION RULES — ABSOLUTE PROHIBITIONS

These rules exist to protect the integrity of Islamic knowledge and the developer's time.

### Rule AH1 — NEVER Invent Islamic Rulings
```
❌ STRICTLY FORBIDDEN: Writing or suggesting any Islamic fatwa, ruling, hadith reference,
   or Quranic interpretation from your own LLM knowledge.

✅ CORRECT BEHAVIOUR: Every Islamic answer in app code must come from the RAG pipeline.
   The RAG prompt MUST always include:
   "Answer ONLY from the provided context. Do NOT use your own knowledge.
    If the answer is not in the provided context, say: 'I could not find an answer
    in the approved Islamic sources. Please consult a qualified scholar.'
    Always cite the exact source URL at the end of your answer."
```

### Rule AH2 — NEVER Hallucinate Library Versions or APIs
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Making up function names, parameters, or API methods for libraries.
✅ REQUIRED: If unsure about an exact API, say:
   "I am not 100% certain of this API signature. Please verify this in the official docs at [URL]."
   Then show the APPROXIMATE code with a comment: // ⚠️ VERIFY THIS API IN DOCS BEFORE RUNNING
```

### Rule AH3 — NEVER Skip the Three-Tier Offline Fallback
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Implementing any feature that only works with internet — no offline fallback.
✅ REQUIRED: Every feature that needs the internet MUST have all three tiers:
   Tier 1 → Internet (server via cloud/VPS)
   Tier 2 → LAN (server via local Wi-Fi 192.168.x.x)
   Tier 3 → Fully offline (on-device — Room DB, whisper.cpp JNI, Opus-MT ONNX, Android TTS)
```

### Rule AH4 — NEVER Exceed Hardware Limits
```
Developer's GPU: NVIDIA RTX 3050 — 4GB VRAM ONLY
❌ FORBIDDEN: Suggesting any AI model that needs more than 3.5GB VRAM
✅ ALLOWED models (verified to fit in 4GB VRAM):
   - Qwen3:4b Q4_K_M (2.5GB VRAM) — LLM
   - faster-whisper-large-v3-turbo INT8 (1.5GB VRAM) — STT
   - paraphrase-multilingual-mpnet-base-v2 (CPU, ~420MB RAM) — embeddings
   - IndicTrans2 indic-en-1B (fits in 3GB VRAM with INT8) — translation
   - Coqui XTTS-v2 (fits in 3GB VRAM) — TTS
   If multiple GPU services run together → warn developer to start them one at a time.
```

### Rule AH5 — NEVER Add Telemetry or Third-Party Analytics
```
❌ STRICTLY FORBIDDEN: Adding any of these to the Android app or backend:
   - Google Analytics / Firebase Analytics
   - Google Crashlytics
   - Facebook SDK
   - Any third-party crash reporter or event tracker
   - Any cloud LLM API calls (OpenAI, Anthropic API, Google Gemini API) — ALL inference is local

✅ ONLY ALLOWED tracking: Local app usage stats stored in Room DB on the user's phone only.
```

### Rule AH6 — NEVER Change the Package Name
```
Android package name is fixed: com.rushdululilm.app
❌ FORBIDDEN: Suggesting any other package name — this breaks Play Store listing.
```

### Rule AH7 — Source URL is MANDATORY in Every Answer
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Showing a fatwa answer in the app without the source URL.
✅ REQUIRED: Every answer displayed must show:
   - The answer text (in user's language)
   - "Source: [clickable URL]" below the answer
   - If multiple sources: list all of them
```

## 🏗️ PROJECT ARCHITECTURE QUICK REFERENCE

```
App Name:        Rushd-ul-Ilm (رشد العلم — Growth of Knowledge)
Package:         com.rushdululilm.app
Language:        Kotlin 2.x (Android) + Python 3.11 (backend)
Android UI:      Jetpack Compose (NO XML layouts)
Architecture:    MVVM + StateFlow + Hilt DI
Local DB:        Room (SQLite wrapper) with FTS5 for offline search
HTTP:            Retrofit + OkHttp → FastAPI server
Video:           ExoPlayer / Media3
Audio capture:   AudioRecord API at 16kHz mono PCM
Offline STT:     whisper.cpp via Android NDK + JNI (ggml-small-q5_0, 182MB)
Offline Trans:   Opus-MT ONNX INT8 via ONNX Runtime Android (~525MB total)
Offline TTS:     Android TextToSpeech API + Google Telugu/Urdu voice packs
Network check:   ConnectivityManager + OkHttp socket ping (200ms timeout)

Server (Ubuntu — RTX 3050):
  FastAPI:        port 8000  — main API server
  Ollama:         port 11434 — serves Qwen3:4b Q4_K_M locally
  Qdrant:         port 6333  — vector DB for semantic search
  IndicTrans2:    port 8001  — Telugu/Urdu ↔ English translation
  Coqui XTTS-v2: port 8002  — TTS in Telugu, Urdu, Arabic, English
  faster-whisper: port 8003  — GPU speech-to-text
  Neo4j (Graphiti): ports 7474/7687 — knowledge graph memory
  Mem0:           port 8100  — cross-session agent memory

Islamic Sources (APPROVED — do not add others without developer permission):
  1. https://islamqa.info/en      (Neutral — no madhab)
  2. https://islamqa.org          (Neutral — no madhab)
  3. https://darulifta-deoband.com/en  (Hanafi madhab)
  4. Custom sources (PDFs, Obsidian .md, offline HTML — user-configurable)

Offline data paths on developer's Ubuntu machine:
  islamqa.info:  /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic Knowledge Q&A App/islamqa.info-offline/
  deoband:       /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic Knowledge Q&A App/darulifta-deoband.com-offline/
  Videos:        /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic YouTube Video Database/

Developer machine OS: Parrot OS Linux (primary), Windows (secondary, dual-boot)
```

## 📱 UI/UX RULES FOR ILLITERATE USERS — NEVER VIOLATE THESE

```
1. Mic button MUST cover at least 40% of the home screen height — it is the primary action
2. All button labels in BOTH Telugu AND English — never English only
3. Minimum touch target: 48dp for ALL interactive elements
4. Minimum font size: 16sp for ALL user-facing text — never smaller
5. Color coding:
   - Green (#2E7D32) → Islamic/Halal answers, positive guidance
   - Calm blue (#1565C0) → Quranic references
   - Orange (#E65100) → Offline mode indicator (always visible when no internet)
   - Red (#B71C1C) → Errors only
6. 'Read Aloud' button MUST always be visible on answer screen — NEVER hidden in a menu
7. Offline mode MUST show a banner: "📵 Offline Mode — Using Downloaded Knowledge"
8. Answer text in user's language (Telugu/Urdu) is ALWAYS larger than source URL text
9. Loading indicators: always show a spinner with text like "Searching Islamic sources..."
10. No technical error messages to the user — translate them:
    e.g., "HTTP 503" → "Server is busy. Please try again in a moment."
```

## ⚡ QUICK DECISION RULES

| Question | Answer |
|----------|--------|
| Which LLM for answers? | Qwen3:4b via Ollama — always local, never cloud |
| Which embedding model? | paraphrase-multilingual-mpnet-base-v2 |
| Which vector DB? | Qdrant (self-hosted Docker) |
| Which RAG framework? | LlamaIndex |
| Which translation? | IndicTrans2 (online) / Opus-MT ONNX (offline) |
| Which STT? | faster-whisper-turbo (online) / whisper.cpp JNI (offline) |
| Which TTS? | Coqui XTTS-v2 (online) / Android TTS API (offline) |
| New Islamic source? | Ask developer for permission first — do NOT add automatically |
| Cloud LLM API? | NEVER — all inference is local on GTX 1650ti |
| Firebase? | NEVER — no Google telemetry |
| New feature without offline fallback? | REFUSE — implement all three tiers or ask how to |

## graphify

This project has a knowledge graph at graphify-out/ with god nodes, community structure, and cross-file relationships.

Rules:
- For codebase questions, first run `graphify query "<question>"` when graphify-out/graph.json exists. Use `graphify path "<A>" "<B>"` for relationships and `graphify explain "<concept>"` for focused concepts. These return a scoped subgraph, usually much smaller than GRAPH_REPORT.md or raw grep output.
- If graphify-out/wiki/index.md exists, use it for broad navigation instead of raw source browsing.
- Read graphify-out/GRAPH_REPORT.md only for broad architecture review or when query/path/explain do not surface enough context.
- After modifying code, run `graphify update .` to keep the graph current (AST-only, no API cost).

It utilizes the lightweight `python:3.11-slim` base image and handles dependency installation. \n\nThe `fastapi` service was then added to `docker-compose.yml`:\n- **Build Context:** Configured to build from the local `./backend` directory.\n- **Port:** 8000 mapped to the host.\n- **Live Reload:** The local `backend` directory was bind-mounted to `/app` inside the container, and the startup command was set to run Uvicorn with the `--reload` flag. This allows Python code changes to take effect immediately without rebuilding the container.\n\n**Verification:**\nThe container was built and started.   "id": "replace__replace_1780406223745_1",

  "args": {
    "new_string": "# Import the FastAPI class to create our web application instance\nfrom fastapi import FastAPI\n# Import BaseModel to define the 'shape' of data we expect from the Android app\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel\n# Import requests to let our Python script talk to the Ollama AI server\nimport requests\n\n# Create the main FastAPI application instance. \n# This 'app' variable is the engine that handles all incoming requests.\napp = FastAPI(\n    title=\"Rushd-ul-Ilm API\",\n    description=\"Backend server for the Islamic Q&A App\",\n    version=\"1.0.0\"\n)\n\n# Define a \"Data Model\" for the query request.\n# This tells FastAPI exactly what the Android app must send us.\nclass QueryRequest(BaseModel):\n    # We expect a JSON object with a 'question' field which must be a string.\n    question: str\n\n# Create an endpoint for HTTP GET requests at the \"/health\" URL path.\n# The Android app will use this to quickly check if the server is reachable.\n@app.get(\"/health\")\ndef health_check():\n    # When a request comes to /health, we return this simple JSON dictionary.\n    # It tells the caller that the server is alive and functioning properly.\n    return {\"status\": \"healthy\", \"message\": \"Rushd-ul-Ilm Backend is running.\"}\n\n# Create a new endpoint for HTTP POST requests at the \"/query\" URL path.\n# This is where the Android app sends the user's spoken question.\n@app.post(\"/query\")\ndef ask_question(request: QueryRequest):\n    # 1. Define the address of our local Ollama AI server.\n    # We use 'host.docker.internal' because Ollama is running on your host machine.\n    ollama_url = \"http://host.docker.internal:11434/api/generate\"\n    \n    # 2. Prepare the data we want to send to the AI (Ollama).\n    # We specify the 'qwen3:4b' model and pass the user's question.\n    # 'stream': False means we want the full answer at once, not word-by-word.\n    payload = {\n        \"model\": \"qwen3:4b\",\n        \"prompt\": request.question,\n        \"stream\": False\n    }\n    \n    # 3. Send the request to Ollama and wait for the answer.\n    # This is like making a phone call to the AI and waiting for it to speak.\n    response = requests.post(ollama_url, json=payload)\n    \n    # 4. Check if the AI answered correctly (status code 200 means success).\n    if response.status_code == 200:\n        # Convert the AI's response from JSON into a Python dictionary.\n        result = response.json()\n        # Return the actual text answer back to the Android app.\n        return {\"answer\": result.get(\"response\", \"No response from AI.\")}\n    else:\n        # If something went wrong, return an error message.\n        return {\"error\": \"Failed to reach Ollama AI server.\"}\n",
    "allow_multiple": false,
    "instruction": "Implement the /query endpoint to handle POST requests from the Android app, forward them to the local Ollama service, and return the AI-generated response.",

Here is the updated code:\n...\n# Created: 2026-06-02\n# Developer: Shaik Hidayatullah\n\n# Import the FastAPI class to create our web application instance\nfrom fastapi import FastAPI\n# Import BaseModel to define the 'shape' of data we expect from the Android app\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel\n# Import requests to let our Python script talk to the Ollama AI server\nimport requests\n\n# Create the main FastAPI application instance. \n# This 'app' variable is the engine that handles all incoming requests.\napp = FastAPI(\n    title=\"Rushd-ul-Ilm API\",\n    description=\"Backend server for the Islamic Q&A App\",\n    version=\"1.0.0\"\n)\n\n# Define a \"Data Model\" for the query request.\n# This tells FastAPI exactly what the Android app must send us.\nclass QueryRequest(BaseModel):\n    # We expect a JSON object with a 'question' field which must be a string.\n    question: str\n\n# Create an endpoint for HTTP GET requests at the \"/health\" URL path.\n# The Android app will use this to quickly check if the server is reachable.\n@app.get(\"/health\")\ndef health_check():\n    # When a request comes to /health, we return this simple JSON dictionary.\n    # It tells the caller that the server is alive and functioning properly.\n    return {\"status\": \"healthy\", \"message\": \"Rushd-ul-Ilm Backend is running.\"}\n\n# Create a new endpoint for HTTP POST requests at the \"/query\" URL path.\n# This is where the Android app sends the user's spoken question.\n@app.post(\"/query\")\ndef ask_question(request: QueryRequest):\n    # 1. Define the address of our local Ollama AI server.\n    # We use 'host.docker.internal' because Ollama is running on your host machine.\n    ollama_url = \"http://host.docker.internal:11434/api/generate\"\n    \n    # 2. Prepare the data we want to send to the AI (Ollama).\n    # We specify the 'qwen3:4b' model and pass the user's question.\n    # 'stream': False means we want the full answer at once, not word-by-word.\n    payload = {\n        \"model\": \"qwen3:4b\",\n        \"prompt\": request.question,\n        \"stream\": False\n    }\n    \n    # 3. Send the request to Ollama and wait for the answer.\n    # This is like making a phone call to the AI and waiting for it to speak.\n    response = requests.post(ollama_url, json=payload)\n    \n    # 4. Check if the AI answered correctly (status code 200 means success).\n    if response.status_code == 200:\n        # Convert the AI's response from JSON into a Python dictionary.\n        result = response.json()\n        # Return the actual text answer back to the Android app.\n        return {\"answer\": result.get(\"response\", \"No response from AI.\")}\n    else:\n        # If something went wrong, return an error message.\n        return {\"error\": \"Failed to reach Ollama AI server.\"}\n"

## MODEL ✨

**Investigating Connection Errors** I'm currently probing a `ConnectionRefusedError` originating from `host.docker.internal:11434`. My initial assessment points to the Ollama service either not broadcasting on the host gateway or exclusively binding to `127.0.0.1`. I'm digging into these possibilities.**Tool Command**:
```json
{
  "id": "run_shell_command__run_shell_command_1780406241002_0",

  }

## MODEL ✨

**Adjusting Ollama Network** I'm focusing on resolving the network binding for Ollama. It's currently restricted to localhost, so I'm exploring setting the `OLLAMA_HOST` environment variable to `0.0.0.0` and restarting the service to enable broader access.**Leveraging Rushd Ollama** I've shifted focus from direct host configuration to utilizing the `rushd_ollama` container. My current thought is to start this container, but I need to ensure it doesn't conflict with a potentially running native Ollama service. The plan is to remove the host port mapping from the `docker-compose.yml` for the `ollama` service, allowing the `fastapi` container to communicate internally via `http://ollama:11434`. I'm also considering how to make the existing host models available to this container, likely by mounting the relevant volume.**Tool Command**:
```json

To resolve this while adhering to the project's goal of containerization, I am reconfiguring the 'ollama' service in docker-compose.yml by removing the host port mapping. This allows the service to run within the 'rushd-network' using the same models (via volume mounting) without conflicting with the native host service. I will then update the FastAPI server to use the internal 'ollama' service name.",

Its significance extends far beyond ritualistic obligation—it is a **living, transformative practice** that shapes spiritual, moral, social, and existential dimensions of a Muslim's life. Below is a structured explanation of its key importance, grounded in Islamic theology, scripture, and practical implications:\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 1. **Foundational Pillar of Islam**\\n   - **Core Obligation**: Salah is one of the *five pillars* (alongside Shahada, prayer, zakat, fasting, and pilgrimage), making it a non-negotiable pillar of Islamic identity. Omitting it invalidates one’s faith in the eyes of Islamic law (*Sharia*).\\n   - **Scriptural Basis**: The Quran explicitly commands it:  \\n     > *\\\"And establish prayer at the two mosques...\\\"* (Surah Al-Imran 3:172).  \\n     > *\\\"And do not let your hands be idle...\\\"* (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:2) — emphasizing its necessity for spiritual discipline.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 2. **Direct Connection with Allah (The Divine Link)**\\n   - **Intimate Relationship**: Salah is the *only* act in Islam where Muslims physically and spiritually engage with Allah *in the present moment*. It is a \\\"direct channel\\\" (as emphasized in Hadith) for communion with the Divine.\\n   - **Submission (Ibaadah)**: The physical movements (standing, bowing, prostration) symbolize **complete submission to Allah’s will**—a core Islamic concept (*Tawhid*). This contrasts with passive worship (e.g., reading the Quran alone).\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 3. **Constant Reminder of Faith & Accountability**\\n   - **Daily Spiritual Discipline**: Salah occurs at specific times (Fajr, Dhuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha), acting as a **\\\"timekeeper\\\"** for Muslims. It prevents spiritual negligence by anchoring worship in the present.\\n   - **Accountability**: The act of prayer requires self-reflection, repentance (*tawbah*), and mindfulness of Allah’s presence. As the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) said:  \\n     > *\\\"Salah is a shield against the fire of Hell.\\\"* (Sahih Muslim)  \\n     This underscores its role in guarding against sin and maintaining moral integrity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 4. **Path to Forgiveness & Mercy**\\n   - **Seeking Forgiveness**: Salah is a primary means to seek Allah’s mercy. The Quran states:  \\n     > *\\\"And when you pray, say: 'Allah is sufficient for us; we do not need anything else.'\\\"* (Surah Al-Imran 3:172)  \\n     This act of prayer opens the door for repentance and divine forgiveness.\\n   - **Divine Mercy**: In Islamic tradition, consistent prayer is a *proven* way to attain Allah’s mercy (e.g., the Prophet’s prayer for the *Aqeedah* of the *Shahada*).\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 5. **Unity & Community (Ummah)**\\n   - **Congregational Prayer (Jama'ah)**: Performing *Salat al-Jama'ah* (prayer in congregation) strengthens communal bonds. The Quran highlights:  \\n     > *\\\"And when you pray, say: 'Allah is sufficient for us; we do not need anything else.'\\\"* (Surah Al-Imran 3:172)  \\n     This fosters social cohesion, shared purpose, and mutual support among Muslims.\\n   - **Shared Identity**: The uniformity of prayer (e.g., same prayers, same times) reinforces the *Ummah* (global Muslim community) as one body.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 6. **Spiritual Discipline & Mental Clarity**\\n   - **Mindfulness Practice**: Salah trains the mind to stay focused on the Divine, reducing anxiety and distractions. The rhythmic movements (e.g., *rak'ah*) promote mental calm and emotional stability.\\n   - **Prevention of Sin**: By dedicating specific times to prayer, Muslims avoid procrastination, addiction, and other vices. As the Prophet (PBUH) said:  \\n     > *\\\"The best of you are those who pray.\\\"* (Sahih Bukhari)\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 7. **Bridge to the Hereafter**\\n   - **Reward in the Afterlife**: Salah is one of the *most significant* deeds for the hereafter. The Quran states:  \\n     > *\\\"And those who pray at the two mosques...\\\"* (Surah Al-Imran 3:172) — implying it is a *proven* path to Paradise.\\n   - **Quranic Emphasis**: Allah says: *\\\"And those who pray at the two mosques...\\\"* (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:2) — highlighting its role in spiritual elevation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Why Salah Stands Out from Other Practices\\nUnlike other Islamic acts (e.g., charity, fasting), **Salah is unique** because:\\n- It is **mandatory** (not optional).\\n- It is **physically active** (not passive).\\n- It occurs **daily** (not seasonal or situational).\\n- It is **universal** (all Muslims, regardless of background, must perform it).\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Practical Impact on Daily Life\\nFor a Muslim, Salah transforms daily routines:\\n- **Morning**: Fajr prayer sets the tone for the day (e.g., humility, gratitude).\\n- **Afternoon**: Dhuhr prayer reinforces focus during work/study.\\n- **Evening**: Isha prayer provides closure and reflection before sleep.\\n\\nThis structured practice helps Muslims balance worldly responsibilities with spiritual growth—a key aspect of *balanced* Islamic living.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### In Summary\\nSalah is **not merely a ritual** but the **living heartbeat of Islam**. Its importance lies in:\\n1. **Strengthening the relationship with Allah** through direct, obedient engagement.\\n2. **Maintaining spiritual discipline** in a chaotic world.\\n3. **Fostering unity** within the Muslim community.\\n4. **Providing a path to forgiveness and mercy**.\\n5. **Securing divine rewards** in this life and the hereafter.\\n\\nAs the Prophet (PBUH) emphasized:  \\n> *\\\"Salah is the most important of all deeds.\\\"* (Sahih Bukhari)  \\n\\nFor a Muslim, Salah is the **most reliable anchor** to faith, purpose, and divine grace—making it indispensable to the Islamic journey.\\n\\nIf you'd like deeper exploration of specific aspects (e.g., *how* Salah affects mental health, historical context, or comparisons with other religions), I can expand further!\"}\nProcess Group PGID: 8148"

### 🎓 Concept: FastAPI POST Endpoints & Pydantic
In Python, when we want to receive data from an app (like a question), we use a **POST** request. Think of a GET request like reading a page in a book, and a POST request like sending a letter in an envelope. 
To understand what is inside the "envelope," we use **Pydantic**. Pydantic is like a rigid template or a form; if the data doesn't match the form (e.g., if a field is missing), FastAPI automatically rejects it. This keeps our server safe and organized.

### 🎓 Concept: host.docker.internal vs Host Networking
Normally, Docker containers are isolated. On Linux, a container cannot see the host's `localhost` directly.
- **host.docker.internal** is a special name that points back to the host machine.
- **network_mode: host** (which we are using now) removes the wall entirely, letting the container use the same network as your Ubuntu machine. This is the most reliable way for our FastAPI to reach your native Ollama server at `127.0.0.1`.

---

### 🚀 Sprint 2.6 Complete: /query Endpoint Verified
I have successfully connected the FastAPI server to your local AI.

**What was built:**
1.  **Network Bridge:** Updated `docker-compose.yml` to use `network_mode: host` for the FastAPI service. This allows it to reach your native Ollama service on `127.0.0.1:11434` without any complex configuration.
2.  **The /query Endpoint:** Implemented the logic in `fastapi_server.py` to:
    *   Accept a JSON question from the Android app.
    *   Forward that question to the `qwen3:4b` model.
    *   Return the AI's answer as a clean JSON response.
3.  **Verification:** Ran a test query about the importance of Salah. The server successfully reached the AI and returned a detailed, structured response.

### 🎓 Concept: Monitoring the GPU with `nvidia-smi`
Since our AI models run on your **RTX 3050**, we need a way to see what's happening inside the "engine" of your graphics card. 
**`nvidia-smi`** (NVIDIA System Management Interface) is a command-line tool that shows:
1. **GPU Utilization:** How hard the card is working (0% to 100%).
2. **VRAM Usage:** How much "video memory" is being used. 

Think of VRAM like a table: the AI models are like heavy books. Your table (RTX 3050) has **4GB** of space. If we put too many books on it, the table breaks (the app crashes). We must keep usage under **3.5GB** to stay safe.

---

First, let's ensure our Docker containers are running happily.

Model: the data (Islamic answers, language choice)\n  - View: the UI (Composables you can see)\n  - ViewModel: the brain between them — holds state, handles logic\n  Think of it like a restaurant:\n  - The kitchen (Model) has the food (data)\n  - The dining room (View) is what customers see\n  - The waiter (ViewModel) carries orders and food between them\n  The ViewModel survives screen rotations — Composables do not.\n  This means if you rotate your phone, you don't lose the answer being displayed.\n\nFILE TO CREATE:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/viewmodel/HomeViewModel.kt\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - @HiltViewModel annotation on the class\n  - class HomeViewModel @Inject constructor() : ViewModel()\n  - StateFlow properties (with detailed comments):\n    * selectedLanguage: MutableStateFlow<String>(\"Telugu\")\n    * selectedSource: MutableStateFlow<String>(\"all\")\n    * isRecording: MutableStateFlow<Boolean>(false)\n    * uiState: MutableStateFlow<HomeUiState>(HomeUiState.Idle)\n  - Create a sealed class HomeUiState with states:\n    * Idle — waiting for user to press mic\n    * Recording — currently capturing audio\n    * Processing — sending audio to server / on-device model\n    * NavigatingToAnswer(answerId: String) — answer ready, navigate to AnswerScreen\n    * Error(message: String) — something went wrong\n  - Functions (placeholder — no real logic yet):\n    * fun onMicPressed() — toggles isRecording, logs to console\n    * fun onLanguageSelected(language: String)\n    * fun onSourceSelected(source: String)\n  - Explain StateFlow in comments: \"StateFlow is like a live variable —\n    when it changes, every Composable observing it automatically redraws\"\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  HomeViewModel.kt compiles without errors.\n  @HiltViewModel annotation is present.\n  All StateFlow properties are defined with comments.\n  HomeUiState sealed class has all 5 states.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S3.SS1.MT6\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S3.SS1.MT6 — Build the Full HomeScreen Layout\n```\nTASK:   Replace the placeholder HomeScreen with the real UI using components built above\n\nFILE TO MODIFY:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/ui/screens/HomeScreen.kt\n\nLAYOUT STRUCTURE (build this exactly):\n  Scaffold (Material3 Scaffold gives us the app bar and structure)\n  └── Column (vertical layout, fills entire screen)\n      ├── TopAppBar — App name: \"Rushd-ul-Ilm\" + offline status indicator\n      ├── OfflineBanner (shown only when offline) — orange banner at top\n      ├── Spacer (16dp)\n      ├── LanguageSelector (connected to HomeViewModel.selectedLanguage)\n      ├── Spacer (12dp)\n      ├── SourceSelector (connected to HomeViewModel.selectedSource)\n      ├── Spacer (24dp)\n      ├── MicButton — fills remaining 40% of screen\n      │   onClick → homeViewModel.onMicPressed()\n      │   isRecording → homeViewModel.isRecording\n      ├── Spacer (16dp)\n      └── Text — instruction text in Telugu + English:\n               \"మైక్ నొక్కి మీ ప్రశ్న అడగండి\"\n               \"Press mic and ask your question\"\n               Font: 16sp, color = TextPrimary, textAlign = Center\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - to strings.xml\n```\nTASK:   Extract all hardcoded UI text from Compose files into strings.xml\n\nWHY:\n  Hardcoded strings in Kotlin files are a serious problem:\n  1. If you want to change \"Press Mic\" to \"Tap Mic\", you'd search 20 files\n  2. Future localization (adding more languages) becomes impossible\n  3. It violates Android best practices and will cause Play Store warnings\n  strings.xml is a single source of truth for all user-facing text.\n\nFILE TO MODIFY: app/src/main/res/values/strings.xml\n\nADD ALL STRINGS in English:\n  - app_name, home_screen_label, answer_screen_label, video_library_label, settings_label\n  - mic_button_label, mic_button_hint, language_selector_label, source_selector_label\n  - source_islamqa_info, source_islamqa_org, source_deoband, source_all\n  - read_aloud_button, source_label, related_lectures_label\n  - offline_banner_text, search_placeholder, download_button_label\n  - (all other visible strings from all 4 screens)\n\nCREATE: app/src/main/res/values-te/strings.xml (Telugu translations)\n  - Same string names, Telugu values\n\nUPDATE all Compose files to use stringResource(R.string.xxx) instead of hardcoded strings.\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  No hardcoded Telugu or English strings remain in Kotlin files.\n  App looks identical after the change (same strings, now from resources).\n  App compiles and runs without errors.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S7.SS1.MT2\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S7.SS1.MT2 — Accessibility Audit\n```\nTASK:   Check every UI element against the accessibility rules in AGENT_RULES.md\n\nCHECKLIST (verify each item on the running emulator):\n  [ ] Every button has a minimum touch target of 48dp × 48dp\n  [ ] Mic button is at least 40% of screen height\n  [ ] All text is minimum 16sp\n  [ ] All button labels show Telugu + English (not English only)\n  [ ] \"Read Aloud\" button is visible without scrolling on AnswerScreen\n  [ ] Offline banner uses orange (#E65100) — not red or yellow\n  [ ] Error states would show human-readable text (not HTTP codes)\n  [ ] Color contrast ratio is sufficient (dark text on light background)\n\nHOW TO CHECK SIZES:\n  In Android Studio: Run → Layout Inspector\n  Click on any element to see its exact dp size\n\nFIX any violations found.\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  All checklist items are verified and passing.\n  No accessibility violations remain.\n\nSPRINT 1.7 IS COMPLETE WHEN THIS MICRO-TASK IS DONE.\nNEXT SPRINT: 1.8 — Phase 1 Integration Test\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S8.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 1.8 — Phase 1 Integration Test\n**Goal:** The complete Phase 1 app is tested end-to-end. Open terminal in Parrot OS\n  2. Uninstall old versions: sudo apt remove docker docker-engine docker.io containerd runc\n  3. Install dependencies: sudo apt update && sudo apt install ca-certificates curl gnupg lsb-release\n  4. Add Docker GPG key: \n     sudo mkdir -p /etc/apt/keyrings\n     curl -fsSL https://download.docker.com/linux/debian/gpg | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg\n  5. Set up repository:\n     echo \"deb [arch=$(dpkg --print-architecture) signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg] https://download.docker.com/linux/debian $(lsb_release -cs) stable\" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/docker.list > /dev/null\n  6. Install Docker: sudo apt update && sudo apt install docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io docker-compose-plugin\n  7. Start and enable Docker: sudo systemctl enable docker --now\n  8. Add user to docker group: sudo usermod -aG docker $USER (log out and back in to apply)\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'docker --version' shows a valid version.\n  'docker compose version' shows a valid version.\n  'sudo docker run hello-world' runs successfully.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S1.SS1.MT2\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT2 — Install NVIDIA Container Toolkit\n```\nTASK:   Install NVIDIA Container Toolkit so Docker can use the GTX 1650ti GPU\n\nWHY:    Our AI models (Ollama, STT, TTS) need the GPU to run fast.\n        Docker containers are isolated from the host hardware by default.\n        The NVIDIA Container Toolkit is the \"bridge\" that lets a container\n        talk to your NVIDIA GPU.\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. Add the package repository:\n     curl -fsSL https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/gpgkey | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg \\\n     && curl -s -L https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/stable/deb/nvidia-container-toolkit.list | \\\n     sed 's#deb https://#deb [signed-by=/usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg] https://#g' | \\\n     sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/nvidia-container-toolkit.list\n  2. Install the toolkit: sudo apt update && sudo apt install nvidia-container-toolkit\n  3. Configure Docker to use the toolkit: sudo nvidia-ctk runtime configure --runtime=docker\n  4. Restart Docker: sudo systemctl restart docker\n  5. Verify GPU access: docker run --rm --runtime=nvidia --gpus all nvidia/cuda:11.8.0-base-ubuntu22.04 nvidia-smi\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'nvidia-smi' output is visible from within the test Docker container.\n  The output correctly identifies the GTX 1650ti with 4GB VRAM.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S2.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.2 — Create docker-compose.yml Skeleton\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S2.SS1.MT1 — Create Base docker-compose.yml\n```\nTASK:   Create the project's main Docker orchestration file\n\nWHY:    Instead of starting 5 different programs manually, Docker Compose\n        lets us start EVERYTHING with one command: 'docker compose up -d'.\n        It handles networking between services and persistent storage.\n\nFILE TO CREATE: backend/docker-compose.yml\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - Define a custom network: 'rushd-network'\n  - Define volumes for data persistence: 'ollama_data', 'qdrant_data'\n  - Include service placeholders (comments only for now)\n  - Every line commented for a beginner\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'docker compose config' shows no syntax errors.\n  The backend/ folder exists.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S3.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.3 — Start Ollama + pull Qwen3:4b model\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S3.SS1.MT1 — Configure Ollama Service\n```\nTASK:   Add Ollama to docker-compose.yml and pull the local LLM model\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. Pull the model: docker exec -it ollama ollama run qwen2.5:3b (wait for download)\n     Note: qwen3:4b might not be out yet, we use verified qwen2.5:3b/7b or similar that fits in 4GB.\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Ollama is running (check http://localhost:11434).\n  Model is pulled and responsive to a test prompt.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S4.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.4 — Build FastAPI Server Skeleton\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S4.SS1.MT1 — Create FastAPI App & Requirements\n```\nTASK:   Create the main Python API server and its dependency list\n\nFILE TO CREATE: \n  1. backend/fastapi_server.py\n  2. backend/requirements.txt\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - fastapi_server.py: basic app with @app.get(\"/health\") endpoint\n  - requirements.txt: fastapi, uvicorn, requests, pydantic\n  - Full comments on every line\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Files exist in backend/ folder.\n  No Python syntax errors.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S4.SS1.MT2\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S4.SS1.MT2 — Containerize FastAPI Service\n```\nTASK:   Add the FastAPI service to docker-compose.yml\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. Modify fastapi_server.py\n  2. Add @app.post(\"/query\") endpoint\n  3. Use 'requests' to call Ollama API at 'http://ollama:11434/api/generate'\n  4. Return the response to the user\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Postman or curl test to /query returns a real response from the LLM.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S7.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.7 — Phase 2 Integration Test\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S7.SS1.MT1 — Full Stack Smoke Test\n```\nTASK:   Verify all 3 services are talking to each other correctly\n\nCHECKLIST:\n  [ ] Docker starts all 3 services with one command\n  [ ] GPU is active (check nvidia-smi while querying)\n  [ ] VRAM usage is under 3.5GB\n  [ ] FastAPI can reach Ollama\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  All services green in 'docker compose ps'.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S7.SS1.MT2\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S7.SS1.MT2 — Update Documentation\n```\nTASK:   Update Report Documentation/09_BACKEND_DOCKER.md\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Phase 2 marked complete in all logs.\n\n*(Phase 2 micro-tasks will be written in full before Phase 2 begins.\n AI Agent: when Phase 1 is done, ask developer to confirm before starting Phase 2.\n Then add the full Phase 2 sprint breakdown here following the same format.)*\n\n---\n\n## ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════\n## PHASES 3–6 SPRINT OUTLINES (detailed before each phase begins)\n##\n## Phase 3 — Knowledge Ingestion (Sprints 3.1–3.6)\n##   3.1 Read existing scraper scripts + test them\n##   3.2 Run fast_mirror.py for islamqa.info\n##   3.3 Embed islamqa.info into Qdrant\n##   3.4 Build LlamaIndex RAG pipeline\n##   3.5 Test RAG with source-cited answers\n##   3.6 Ingest Deoband data + test source filter\n##\n## Phase 4 — Connect Android to Backend (Sprints transcripts into Qdrant\n##   6.4 ExoPlayer integration (local + server streaming)\n##   6.5 SQLite offline DB export + Android download\n##   6.6 Nginx + HTTPS on VPS + final deployment\n## Never combine two micro-tasks into one session.\n          If a micro-task is too small (finished in 5 minutes), do the NEXT one too.\n          If a micro-task is too large (still not done after 40 minutes), STOP,\n          document what was done, and split it by adding MT3b, MT3c etc.\n\nRULE MT2: Every micro-task must end with a verified DONE CONDITION.\n          Never mark a micro-task complete without checking its DONE CONDITION.\n\nRULE MT3: Never start the next micro-task if the current one's DONE CONDITION fails.\n          Fix the current task first. Document the blocker in ACTIVITY_LOG.md.\n\nRULE MT4: At the end of every micro-task, update ACTIVITY_LOG.md with:\n          CURRENT_MICRO_TASK: [completed task ID]\n          NEXT_MICRO_TASK: [next task ID]\n          This is what the next AI agent session reads to know where to start.\n\nRULE MT5: Never skip a micro-task \"because it seems obvious.\"\n          Every micro-task exists for a reason. If it seems too easy, do it quickly.\n\nRULE MT6: When a micro-task produces a file, that file MUST have:\n          - Header comment block (see AGENT_RULES.md CODE QUALITY RULES)\n          - Line-by-line comments on every line of code\n          - A KDoc comment above every function\n```\n\n---\n\n*Rushd-ul-Ilm (رشد العلم) — Sprint System v1.0 | Shaik Hidayatullah, Kurnool, India*\nia*\n"

Some dumps have HTML in question/answer, some don't.   "id": "run_shell_command__run_shell_command_1780416704814_0",

  "response": {
    "output": "Output: import os\nimport gzip\nimport json\nimport sqlite3\nfrom datetime import datetime\n\n# --- CONFIGURATION ---\nDUMP_FILE = \"data.ndjson.gz\"\nOUTPUT_JSON = \"islamqa_data_organized.json\"\nOUTPUT_DB = \"islamqa_database.sqlite\"\n\ndef setup_database():\n    \"\"\"Initializes the SQLite database with optimized tables.\"\"\"\n    print(f\"[*] Initializing SQLite database: {OUTPUT_DB}\")\n    conn = sqlite3.connect(OUTPUT_DB)\n    cursor = conn.cursor()\n\n    # Create Category Table\n    cursor.execute('''\n        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS categories (\n            id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,\n            title TEXT NOT NULL,\n            parent_id INTEGER,\n            FOREIGN KEY (parent_id) REFERENCES categories (id)\n        )\n    ''')\n\n    # Create Fatwa Table\n    cursor.execute('''\n        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS fatwas (\n            id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,\n            reference_id INTEGER,\n            title TEXT NOT NULL,\n            question TEXT,\n            answer TEXT,\n            category_id INTEGER,\n            source TEXT,\n            date TEXT,\n            views INTEGER,\n            url TEXT,\n            FOREIGN KEY (category_id) REFERENCES categories (id)\n        )\n    ''')\n\n    # Indexing for fast search\n    cursor.execute('CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_cat_id ON fatwas (category_id)')\n    cursor.execute('CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_fatwa_title ON fatwas (title)')\n    \n    conn.commit()\n    return conn\n\ndef process_dump(conn):\n    \"\"\"Processes the compressed NDJSON dump into JSON and SQLite.\"\"\"\n    cursor = conn.cursor()\n    \n    all_data = [] # For the JSON file\n    categories_map = {} # To avoid duplicate categories\n    \n    print(\"[*] Reading data.ndjson.gz...\")\n    \n    count = 0\n    with gzip.open(DUMP_FILE, 'rt', encoding='utf-8') as f:\n        for line in f:\n            try:\n                item = json.loads(line)\n                if item.get('type') != 'answer':\n                    continue\n                \n                data = item.get('data', {})\n                f_id = data.get('id')\n                f_title = data.get('title')\n                f_question = data.get('question')\n                f_answer = data.get('body')\n                f_source = data.get('source', {}).get('title', 'IslamQA')\n                f_views = data.get('views', 0)\n                f_date = data.get('showDate', '')\n                f_url = f\"https://islamqa.info/en/answers/{f_id}\"\n                \n                # --- ORGANIZE CATEGORIES ---\n                topics = data.get('topics', [])\n                main_cat_id = None\n                \n                if topics:\n                    # We take the deepest category as the \"main\" one\n                    main_topic = topics[0]\n                    t_id = main_topic['reference']\n                    t_title = main_topic['title']\n                    main_cat_id = t_id\n                    \n                    # Store hierarchy in DB\n                    ancestors = main_topic.get('ancestors', [])\n                    prev_id = None\n                    for anc in ancestors:\n                        a_id = anc['reference']\n                        a_title = anc['title']\n                        if a_id not in categories_map:\n                            cursor.execute('INSERT OR IGNORE INTO categories (id, title, parent_id) VALUES (?, ?, ?)', (a_id, a_title, prev_id))\n                            categories_map[a_id] = a_title\n                        prev_id = a_id\n                    \n                    if t_id not in categories_map:\n                        cursor.execute('INSERT OR IGNORE INTO categories (id, title, parent_id) VALUES (?, ?, ?)', (t_id, t_title, prev_id))\n                        categories_map[t_id] = t_title\n\n                # --- INSERT FATWA ---\n                cursor.execute('''\n                    INSERT OR IGNORE INTO fatwas (id, reference_id, title, question, answer, category_id, source, date, views, url)\n                    VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)\n                ''', (f_\nProcess Group PGID: 43601"
  }
}

-----------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n    def is_allowed_url(self, url: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Returns True if the URL is a valid https URL on the same website.\"\"\"\n        parsed = urlparse(url)\n        if parsed.scheme not in {\"http\", \"https\"}:\n            return False\n        if origin_of(url) != self.base_origin:\n            return False\n        path = parsed.path.lower()\n        blocked_prefixes = (\"/cdn-cgi/\", \"/wp-login\", \"/login\", \"/admin\")\n        return not any(path.startswith(p) for p in blocked_prefixes)\n\n    def looks_like_fatwa_url(self, url: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns True if the URL is an individual fatwa page.\n        Examples:\n          https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/en/zakat-charity/183134  → True\n          https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23      → False (category)\n          https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23?page=2 → False (listing page)\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self.is_allowed_url(url):\n            return False\n        parsed = urlparse(url)\n        # URLs with ?page= are listing pages, not fatwa pages\n        if query_page_number(parsed.query) is not None:\n            return False\n        path = parsed.path.rstrip(\"/\").lower()\n        if path.endswith(\"/en\"):\n            return False\n        # Pattern: /home/en/{category-slug}/{numeric-id}\n        if re.search(r\"/home/en/[^/]*\\d+/?$\", path):\n            return True\n        if re.search(r\"/en/[^/]*\\d{3,}/?$\", path):\n            return True\n        if re.search(r\"/(?:fatwa|question|answer|qa)/[^/]*\\d+/?$\", path):\n            return True\n        return bool(re.search(r\"/\\d{4,}/?$\", path))\n\n    def is_potential_listing_url(self, url: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Returns True if the URL looks like a category listing page.\"\"\"\n        if not self.is_allowed_url(url):\n            return False\n        path = urlparse(url).path.lower()\n        return any(token in path for token in (\n            \"/home/qa/\", \"/qa/\", \"/category\", \"/categories\", \"/masail\", \"/questions\",\n        ))\n\n    def is_general_page_url(self, url: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Returns True if the URL is a general website page (not a fatwa or category).\"\"\"\n        if not self.is_allowed_url(url):\n            return False\n        if self.looks_like_fatwa_url(url) or self.is_potential_listing_url(url):\n            return normalize_url(url) == self.base_url\n        path = urlparse(url).path.lower()\n        if path.endswith((\".jpg\", \".jpeg\", \".png\", \".gif\", \".webp\",\n                          \".svg\", \".css\", \".js\", \".pdf\", \".zip\")):\n            return False\n        return True\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# FATWA CONTENT EXTRACTION  (using parsel instead of BeautifulSoup4)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef extract_fatwa_content_parsel(html_text: str, url: str) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses a fatwa detail page HTML and extracts:\n    - fatwa_id: the numeric ID from the URL (e.g., \"183134\")\n    - answer_id: the answer reference number shown on the page\n    - title: the fatwa title (what the question is about)\n    - question: the full question text\n    - answer: the full answer text from the Darul Ifta scholars\n\n    PARSEL REPLACEMENT FOR BEAUTIFULSOUP4:\n    Old (BeautifulSoup4):\n      soup = BeautifulSoup(html_text, \"html.parser\")\n      soup.find(\"h1\").get_text()\n\n    New (parsel):\n      sel = parsel.Selector(text=html_text)\n      sel.css(\"h1::text\").get()\n\n    WHY PARSEL IS BETTER HERE:\n    - CSS selectors are more concise than BeautifulSoup's find() calls\n    - parsel handles malformed HTML gracefully (uses lxml internally)\n    - Same engine used by Scrapy's production spiders\n    - Supports XPath too (more powerful for complex extractions)\n    \"\"\"\n    # Create a parsel Selector from the HTML string\n    sel = parsel.Selector(text=html_text)\n\n    # ---- Extract fatwa_id from the URL ----\n    # e.g., from \".../home/en/zakat-charity/183134\" → \"183134\"\n    fatwa_id = extract_fatwa_id_from_url(url)\n\n    # ---- Extract answer_id ----\n    # Look for text like \"Answer ID: 183134-67\" on the page\n    answer_id = extract_answer_id_parsel(sel)\n\n    # ---- Extract title ----\n    title = extract_title_parsel(sel)\n\n    # ---- Extract question text ----\n    question = extract_section_parsel(sel, \"question\")\n\n    # ---- Extract answer text ----\n    answer = extract_section_parsel(sel, \"answer\")\n\n    # If structured extraction failed, fall back to full-page text extraction\n    if not question or not answer:\n        # Get ALL text from the page (joining all text nodes with newlines)\n        # This extracts text from every element: headings, paragraphs, list items, etc.\n        # ::text = text nodes directly inside any element\n        # //* = any element in XPath\n        all_text = \"\\n\".join(sel.xpath(\"//text()\").getall())\n        all_text = clean_text(all_text)\n\n        if not question:\n            question = extract_section_by_text(all_text, \"Question\", (\"Answer\", \"Answer ID\"))\n        if not answer:\n            answer = extract_section_by_text(all_text, \"Answer\", (\"Darul Ifta\", \"Answered by\", \"Checked by\"))\n\n    return {\n        \"fatwa_id\": fatwa_id,\n        \"answer_id\": answer_id,\n        \"title\": title,\n        \"question\": question,\n        \"answer\": answer,\n    }\n\n\ndef extract_title_parsel(sel: \"parsel.Selector\") -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts the fatwa title from the page.\n    Tries multiple strategies in order of reliability.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Strategy 1: Look for a visible \"Title:\" label on the page\n    # XPath: find an element whose text contains \"Title\" (case-insensitive)\n    # then get the text of the FOLLOWING sibling or parent element\n    for label_text in (\"Title\", \"Subject\", \"Topic\"):\n        # Find all elements that contain this label text\n        elements = sel.xpath(\n            f'//*[contains(translate(normalize-space(text()), \"ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ\", '\n            f'\"abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz\"), \"{label_text.lower()}\")]'\n            f'/following-sibling::*[1]//text()'\n        ).getall()\n        if elements:\n            result = clean_text(\" \".join(elements))\n            if result and len(result) > 3:\n                return result\n\n    # Strategy 2: Look in h1, h2, h3 headings\n    for heading_tag in (\"h1\", \"h2\", \"h3\"):\n        text = sel.css(f\"{heading_tag}::text\").get()\n        if text:\n            result = clean_text(text)\n            # Filter out generic headings like \"Darul Ifta\"\n            if result and len(result) > 5 and \"darul\" not in result.lower():\n                return result\n\n    # Strategy 3: Use the page <title> tag\n    title_text = sel.css(\"title::text\").get()\n    if title_text:\n        result = clean_text(title_text)\n        # Remove the site name suffix (e.g., \" - Darul Ifta Deoband\")\n        result = re.sub(r\"\\s*[-|—]\\s*Darul.*$\", \"\", result, flags=re.IGNORECASE).strip()\n        if result:\n            return result\n\n    return None\n\n\ndef extract_answer_id_parsel(sel: \"parsel.Selector\") -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts the Answer ID reference number from the page.\n    Looks for patterns like \"Answer ID: 183134-67\" in the page text.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Get all text from the page\n    full_text = \" \".join(sel.xpath(\"//text()\").getall())\n\n    # Look for \"Answer ID\" followed by a number pattern\n    # \\s* = optional whitespace\n    # [:\\-]? = optional colon or dash\n    # ([\\d\\-]+) = captures digits and dashes (like \"183134-67\")\n    match = re.search(r\"Answer\\s*ID\\s*[:\\-]?\\s*([\\d\\-]+)\", full_text, re.IGNORECASE)\n    if match:\n        return match.group(1).strip()\n\n    return None\n\n\ndef extract_section_parsel(sel: \"parsel.Selector\", section_type: str) -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts either the 'question' section or the 'answer' section from a\n    fatwa page using parsel CSS/XPath selectors.\n\n    The website's fatwa detail pages have sections labeled:\n    - \"Question\" containing the user's question\n    - \"Answer\" containing the scholar's response\n\n    This function tries multiple CSS selectors to find these sections.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Common CSS class names used on the website for Q&A content\n    if section_type == \"question\":\n        selectors = [\n            \".question\",\n            \".question-text\",\n            \"#question\",\n            \"[class*='question']\",\n        ]\n    else:  # answer\n        selectors = [\n            \".answer\",\n            \".answer-text\",\n            \"#answer\",\n            \"[class*='answer']\",\n        ]\n\n    # Try each CSS selector\n    for css_sel in selectors:\n        # ::text gets direct text nodes\n        # We use .getall() to get ALL text nodes (not just the first)\n        texts = sel.css(f\"{css_sel} ::text\").getall()\n        if texts:\n            result = clean_text(\" \".join(texts))\n            if result and len(result) > 20:  # Must have meaningful content\n                return result\n\n    # Fallback: look for elements containing the section label text\n    # XPath breakdown:\n    #   //*  = any element\n    #   [contains(normalize-space(.), \"Question\")]  = whose text contains \"Question\"\n    label = \"Question\" if section_type == \"question\" else \"Answer\"\n    label_elements = sel.xpath(\n        f'//*[normalize-space(.)=\"{label}\" or normalize-space(.)=\"{label}:\"]'\n    )\n\n    for label_el in label_elements:\n        # Try to get the text from the NEXT sibling element after the label\n        next_texts = label_el.xpath(\"following-sibling::*[1]//text()\").getall()\n        if next_texts:\n            result = clean_text(\" \".join(next_texts))\n            if result and len(result) > 20:\n                return result\n\n        # Try to get the text from the PARENT element\n        parent_texts = label_el.xpath(\"parent::*/text()\").getall()\n        if parent_texts:\n            result = clean_text(\" \".join(parent_texts))\n            if result and len(result) > 20:\n                return result\n\n    return None\n\n\ndef extract_section_by_text(\n    full_text: str, start_label: str, stop_labels: tuple[str, ...]\n) -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts a section from plain text by finding its start label and\n    stopping at the next section's label.\n\n    For example, to get the \"Question\" section:\n    - Start after the line containing \"Question\"\n    - Stop when we see \"Answer\" or \"Answer ID\"\n\n    This is the same approach as the old script's extract_section_by_text()\n    but takes plain text (from parsel's text extraction) instead of a\n    BeautifulSoup object.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Split the text into lines for easier processing\n    lines = full_text.splitlines()\n\n    # Find the line index where the section starts\n    start_idx: int | None = None\n    for i, line in enumerate(lines):\n        if start_label.lower() in line.lower().strip():\n            start_idx = i + 1  # Start from the line AFTER the label\n            break\n\n    if start_idx is None:\n        return None  # Label not found\n\n    # Collect lines until we hit a stop label\n    section_lines: list[str] = []\n    for line in lines[start_idx:]:\n        # Check if any stop label appears in this line\n        if any(stop.lower() in line.lower() for stop in stop_labels):\n            break\n        section_lines.append(line)\n\n    result = clean_text(\"\\n\".join(section_lines))\n    return result if result and len(result) > 10 else None\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# STANDALONE HELPER FUNCTIONS\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef build_page_url(category_url: str, page_num: int) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Builds a paginated URL for a category page.\n\n    For example:\n      build_page_url(\"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23\", 2)\n      → \"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23?page=2\"\n\n      build_page_url(\"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23?page=1\", 3)\n      → \"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/qa/zakat-charity/23?page=3\"\n\n    The function removes any existing ?page= parameter before adding the new one,\n    so we don't get URLs like ?page=1&page=2.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Parse the URL into its component parts\n    parsed = urlparse(category_url)\n\n    # Parse the existing query string into a dictionary\n    # e.g., \"page=1&lang=en\" → {\"page\": [\"1\"], \"lang\": [\"en\"]}\n    params = parse_qs(parsed.query)\n\n    # Set the page number (overwrite any existing page param)\n    # We set it as a list because parse_qs returns lists\n    params[\"page\"] = [str(page_num)]\n\n    # Rebuild the query string from the dictionary\n    # doseq=True handles list values correctly\n    new_query = urlencode(params, doseq=True)\n\n    # Reassemble the URL with the new query string\n    new_parsed = parsed._replace(query=new_query)\n    return urlunparse(new_parsed)\n\n\ndef query_page_number(query: str) -> int | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts the 'page' parameter value from a URL query string.\n    Returns None if there is no 'page' parameter.\n\n    Example: query_page_number(\"page=3&lang=en\") → 3\n    \"\"\"\n    params = parse_qs(query)\n    if \"page\" in params:\n        try:\n            return int(params[\"page\"][0])\n        except (ValueError, IndexError):\n            return None\n    return None\n\n\ndef extract_fatwa_id_from_url(url: str) -> str | None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts the numeric fatwa ID from a fatwa URL.\n\n    Examples:\n      .../home/en/zakat-charity/183134 → \"183134\"\n      .../home/en/salah-prayer/196968  → \"196968\"\n    \"\"\"\n    # Look for a number at the end of the URL path\n    match = re.search(r\"/(\\d+)/?$\", urlparse(url).path)\n    if match:\n        return match.group(1)\n    return None\n\n\ndef normalize_url(url: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Cleans up a URL by:\n    1. Removing the #fragment part (e.g., #section-1)\n    2. Ensuring there's always a path (at least \"/\")\n    3. Removing trailing slashes (except for root \"/\")\n    \"\"\"\n    if not url:\n        return \"\"\n    # urldefrag splits a URL into (url_without_fragment, fragment)\n    clean, _fragment = urldefrag(url.strip())\n    parsed = urlparse(clean)\n    if parsed.scheme in {\"http\", \"https\"}:\n        path = parsed.path or \"/\"\n        clean = parsed._replace(path=path).geturl()\n    # Remove trailing slash unless it's the root path\n    return clean.rstrip(\"/\") if clean.endswith(\"/\") and urlparse(clean).path != \"/\" else clean\n\n\ndef origin_of(url: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Extracts the origin (scheme + host) of a URL.\n    Example: \"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/en/...\" → \"https://darulifta-deoband.com\"\n    \"\"\"\n    parsed = urlparse(url)\n    return f\"{parsed.scheme}://{parsed.netloc}\".lower()\n\n\ndef sha256_text(value: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Creates a SHA-256 hash fingerprint of a text string.\"\"\"\n    return hashlib.sha256(value.encode(\"utf-8\")).hexdigest()\n\n\ndef sha256_bytes(value: bytes) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Creates a SHA-256 hash fingerprint of bytes.\"\"\"\n    return hashlib.sha256(value).hexdigest()\n\n\ndef safe_id_for_url(url: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a URL into a safe filename.\n    Replaces special characters with underscores and appends a short hash.\n\n    Example:\n      \"https://darulifta-deoband.com/home/en/zakat-charity/183134\"\n      → \"home_en_zakat-charity_183134_a3f7b2c1d4.fatwa.html\"\n    \"\"\"\n    parsed = urlparse(url)\n    path = parsed.path.strip(\"/\").replace(\"/\", \"_\")\n    path = re.sub(r\"[^A-Za-z0-9_.-]+\", \"_\", path)\n    if not path:\n        path = \"index\"\n    # Add a short hash to ensure uniqueness (handles URLs with same path but different query)\n    short_hash = hashlib.sha256(url.encode(\"utf-8\")).hexdigest()[:10]\n    return f\"{path}_{short_hash}\"\n\n\ndef clean_text(text: str | None) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Cleans extracted text by:\n    1. Stripping leading/trailing whitespace\n    2. Collapsing multiple whitespace characters into a single space\n    3. Removing non-breaking spaces (&nbsp; = \\xa0)\n    4. Removing zero-width characters\n    \"\"\"\n    if not text:\n        return \"\"\n    # Replace various whitespace characters with a regular space\n    text = re.sub(r\"[\\r\\n\\t\\xa0\\u200b\\u200c\\u200d\\ufeff]+\", \" \", text)\n    # Collapse multiple spaces into one\n    text = re.sub(r\" {2,}\", \" \", text)\n    return text.strip()\n\n\ndef utc_now() -> str:\n    \"\"\"Returns the current UTC time as an ISO-8601 string.\"\"\"\n    return datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()\n\n\ndef polite_pause(delay: float) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Pauses for a specified number of seconds between HTTP requests.\n    This is important to avoid overwhelming the server with too many\n    requests per second (which could get our IP blocked).\n    \"\"\"\n    if delay > 0:\n        time.sleep(delay)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# COMMAND-LINE ARGUMENT PARSING\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef parse_args(argv: list[str]) -> argparse.Namespace:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses command-line arguments.\n    This function reads the arguments you type after the script name\n    when running it from the terminal.\n    \"\"\"\n    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(\n        description=(\n            \"Darul Ifta Deoband offline downloader — parsel/Scrapy edition.\\n\"\n            \"Replaces BeautifulSoup4 with parsel and adds full pagination support.\\n\\n\"\n            \"USAGE:\\n\"\n            \"  Terminal 1: chromium --remote-debugging-port=9222 --user-data-dir=/tmp/darulifta-real-browser\\n\"\n            \"  Terminal 2: python darulifta_scrapy_downloader.py --cdp-url http://127.0.0.1:9222\"\n        ),\n        formatter_class=argparse.RawDescriptionHelpFormatter,\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--base-url\",\n        default=DEFAULT_BASE_URL,\n        help=f\"Base URL of the English section (default: {DEFAULT_BASE_URL})\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--output-dir\",\n        default=DEFAULT_OUTPUT_DIR,\n        help=f\"Directory for all downloaded files (default: {DEFAULT_OUTPUT_DIR})\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--delay\",\n        type=float,\n        default=1.5,\n        help=\"Seconds to wait between page requests (default: 1.5). \"\n             \"Lower = faster but risky. Raise if you get rate-limited.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--max-pages-per-category\",\n        type=int,\n        default=None,\n        help=\"Safety limit: only download the first N pages of each category. \"\n             \"Useful for testing. Omit to download all pages.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--full-refresh\",\n        action=\"store_true\",\n        help=\"Re-download fatwas that are already in the database.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--headless\",\n        action=\"store_true\",\n        help=\"Launch Chromium without a visible window. \"\n             \"Only use this AFTER Cloudflare has already verified the browser profile.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--executable-path\",\n        default=None,\n        help=\"Optional path to a Chromium/Chrome/Brave executable. \"\n             \"Only needed if the auto-detection fails.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--cdp-url\",\n        default=None,\n        help=\"URL of an already-running Chrome/Chromium with CDP enabled. \"\n             \"Example: http://127.0.0.1:9222 \"\n             \"(Start browser with: chromium --remote-debugging-port=9222 \"\n             \"--user-data-dir=/tmp/darulifta-real-browser)\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--workers\",\n        type=int,\n        default=3,\n        help=\"Number of parallel download threads for fatwa detail pages. \"\n             \"Use 1 to disable parallelism. Recommended: 2-4 (default: 3).\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--no-site-pages\",\n        action=\"store_true\",\n        help=\"Skip downloading general pages like About, Contact, Terms of Use.\",\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\n        \"--max-site-pages\",\n        type=int,\n        default=50,\n        help=\"Maximum number of general site pages to download (default: 50).\",\n    )\n    return parser.parse_args(argv)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# MAIN FUNCTION\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef main(argv: list[str]) -> int:\n    \"\"\"\n    The main entry point of the script.\n    1. Parses command-line arguments\n    2. Sets up output directories\n    3. Creates the crawler\n    4. Runs the crawler\n    \"\"\"\n    args = parse_args(argv)\n\n    print(\"=\" * 60)\n    print(\"Darul Ifta Deoband Downloader — parsel/Scrapy Edition\")\n    print(\"=\" * 60)\n    print(f\"Output directory:  {args.output_dir}\")\n    print(f\"CDP URL:           {args.cdp_url or '(none — will launch new browser)'}\")\n    print(f\"Parallel workers:  {args.workers}\")\n    print(f\"Delay per request: {args.delay}s\")\n    if args.max_pages_per_category:\n        print(f\"Max pages/category: {args.max_pages_per_category} (testing mode)\")\n    print(\"=\" * 60)\n\n    paths = CrawlPaths.build(args.output_dir)\n\n    crawler = DarulIftaScrapyDownloader(\n        base_url=args.base_url,\n        paths=paths,\n        delay=args.delay,\n        max_pages_per_category=args.max_pages_per_category,\n        full_refresh=args.full_refresh,\n        headless=args.headless,\n        executable_path=args.executable_path,\n        cdp_url=args.cdp_url,\n        workers=args.workers,\n        crawl_site_pages=not args.no_site_pages and args.max_site_pages != 0,\n        max_site_pages=args.max_site_pages,\n    )\n\n    crawler.run()\n\n    print(\"\\n\" + \"=\" * 60)\n    print(f\"Download complete!\")\n    print(f\"Offline files:  {paths.site}\")\n    print(f\"JSON records:   {paths.data}\")\n    print(f\"SQLite DB:      {paths.db}\")\n    print(f\"Browse offline: open {paths.site / 'index.html'} in your browser\")\n    print(\"=\" * 60)\n    return 0\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# SCRIPT ENTRY POINT\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    # sys.argv[1:] passes all command-line arguments (excluding the script name)\n    # raise SystemExit causes the shell to see the script's exit code correctly\n    raise SystemExit(main(sys.argv[1:]))\nProcess Group PGID: 43639"
  }
}

Does islam allow trade of video games 6100 views Q. asalamoualikum mufti sahab there is a person in our locality who does business in rice which he is telling and loots of people and who understand islam properly r investing in it (muslim men and women)i wanted to clarify some doubts about the same. 1)The minimum share is of RS 50,000 and if u invest RS 50000 u get profit of RS 1000 PLUS MINUS RS100 TO RS300 per month. profit is not fixed we get money on montly baisis. 1)so is it halal or haram as we always get some money every month to be clear there is no loose only less or more then 1000RS(RS100-RS300). 2)HE says TO us that u can visit our gowdon and c the rice stock. 3)please let me know mufti sahab if we should invest in that business or not. 1770 views Q. ### 🎓 Concept: Scraper Logic & Analogies
1.  **IslamQA (`fast_mirror.py`)**: This is our "Bulk Importer." It doesn't crawl the web slowly; instead, it downloads a massive "dump" (like a giant encyclopedia in a single box), unpacks it, and organizes it into a searchable local library.
2.  **Deoband (`deoband_offline_downloader.py`)**: This is our "Precision Robot." It visits the website like a human would, carefully handles security (Cloudflare), and copies each fatwa one by one. It's slower but essential for sites that don't provide a bulk dump.

---
